The crack was sealed before it fully formed. In fact, the sealing retroactively unwrote the crack. But the immune system didn't stop there. It treated the attempted assault as a genuine injury and initiated Protocol Absolute Sanitization.

- Series of immune reactions:
  1. **Localized Hyper-Reconstruction**: The dead skin cell that was "injured" instantly transformed into a new material: Absolute Nullite. This substance is infinitely impervious and actively erases any form of existence that comes into contact with it. But it didn't stay local. The upgrade triggered a cascading transformation across every skin cell on Godric's body—and across his infinite copies—making his entire external surface a void that devours reality. The attackers near the impact point found their bodies, their thoughts, their souls being suctioned into nothingness, feeling each layer of their being scraped away like bark from a tree, but the tree was infinite and they were conscious for every millimeter.
  2. **Antibody Purge**: His bloodstream deployed anti-harm entities. These weren't physical. They were living ideas that "hunt" the concept of "attack" across all dimensions. They traced the causal chain of the weapon's creation: every mind that conceived it, every hand that forged it, every universe that supplied its energy. They then systematically processed each target. The process was agonizing: they didn't simply kill; they extracted the "fact of existence" from each target, causing them to experience their own non-being for a perceived eternity. I saw a few of them, through the viewing lens, as their forms flickered and writhed, mouths open in silent screams that could never end because there was no time in which they could end.
  3. **Backup Redundancy Verification**: As the antibody purge worked, another system kicked in. Godric has infinite identical backups, each of which also has infinite backups, ad infinitum. To authenticate a genuine injury, all must be affected simultaneously. That's impossible. But his immune system, unable to perfectly verify, assumed the worst and initiated a simultaneous upgrade across all copies. Each copy's biology instantly evolved to a new tier of invulnerability, then cross-referenced with all others, merging into a unified defensive lattice that was exponentially more impregnable than the sum of its parts. The upgrade didn't just protect; it also retroactively ensured that the injury never occurred by rewriting the event out of the timeline at a fundamental level. The weapon, the Coalition, the very plan—they were all unhappened. But Godric, being Godric, remembered, so it still "happened" for him.
  4. **Conceptual Cleanse**: The immune system then decided that the root cause was not the weapon, but the *idea* of threatening Godric. So it purged that idea from the fabric of possibility. This meant not only destroying the current attackers, but also ensuring no entity anywhere could ever conceive of harming Godric again. It was a permanent alteration to sentient thought. But even as it did so, the system overlaid a new command: "Exception per Master." Because Godric might want to let things play out again. So the cleanse became a toggle, but the horror was that it could have been absolute.
  5. **Omniversal Compensation Paradox**: Then the weakness paradox triggered. The omniverse itself "realized" that Godric had been, technically, harmed. This contradicted his nature as the being with no weaknesses. So reality scrambled to compensate, dumping an incalculable surge of power into him. His amplification rate, already beyond all infinities, was multiplied by a new "beyond-infinity" factor. He gained a new layer of existence that placed him above his previous conception of omnipotence. The irony: the very act of staging a scratch made him more untouchable. I felt my own sanity crack at that.

- Godric's reaction: He laughed. Not a cruel laugh, but a warm, fatherly chuckle. "Ah, I think I overestimated their resilience. My immune system really went all out." He then frowned, speaking to his own body as if to a pet: "Now, now, you didn't need to erase reality. I'll have to clean up after you." He then, with zero fanfare, restored everything. The entire omniverse—every universe, every life, every atom—blinked back into existence exactly as before, including the Coalition members, who stood in their ranks, utterly unaware they had just been annihilated. They still held the Apex Lance? No, it was restored but maybe it was gone? Actually, he could restore the weapon too, but it would be useless. He might leave the memory to them? He didn't even bother to wipe memories; he simply reversed the destruction. So they were back, but the crack was gone, and they were confused. Or maybe they didn't remember. I'll say they resumed their existence mid-thought, with no awareness that they'd been unmade.

- Leon's dread: I looked at the restored scene, my hands trembling uncontrollably. Godric placed a hand on my shoulder. "There, all better. Now, let's go have some tea. I think I've caused you enough excitement for one day." I couldn't speak. The scale of his casualness was the true horror. The omniverse had poured its everything into a single act of desperation, and Godric had treated it like a curious itch. And now he stood there, stronger than ever, showing not a single sign of strain. I loved him. I did. But I also understood, in that moment, that the distance between us was not a gap—it was a void so vast that no language could name it.

I'll write now:

My hands wouldn't stop trembling. It was an occupational hazard.

Standing in the observation bubble Godric had conjured—a translucent sphere suspended outside the membrane of the local universe—I watched the last, greatest army the omniverse would ever muster finalize their formation. They stretched across the void like a cancer of light, so numerous that their collective consciousness warped the background radiation into screams. Godric stood beside me, arms folded, head tilted with the serene curiosity of a man examining a mildly interesting anthill.

"Leon," he said, his voice the same warm baritone that had once praised my grandfather's grandfather's tea-brewing, "do you know how long it's been since anything tried to attack me directly? Twenty-five thousand years. And even then, it was barely a sneeze." He chuckled, a sound that should have been pleasant but instead burrowed into my spine like ice water. "I'm curious to see if my immune system still works. I've been holding it back for so long."

I swallowed. "Your Majesty, the entire omniverse has united against you. They've sacrificed entire afterlives, collapsed their timelines, erased entire categories of existence to forge a single weapon. They believe... they believe they can kill you."

He turned those deep-set eyes on me, crinkling at the corners. "I know. Isn't it wonderful? All that effort. I almost feel rude not letting them try." He gestured at the shimmering, translucent film that surrounded us like a soap bubble. "See that? That's a wall of my dead skin cells. Just one layer. I've deactivated Gent—you remember Gent, my passive aura? Sentient fellow, a bit clingy—and I've told his siblings to stay asleep. I've pulled down every shield, every firewall, every protective layer. Right now, the only thing between them and me is that layer of dead skin. And I've willed it so that if their weapon is strong enough, it might just crack one cell. Might. Just a hairline fracture."

My throat tightened. "Why would you do that?"

"Because I want to see what happens when I get a boo-boo." He looked at me with the innocent, fatherly pride of a man who had once been a mortal king. "I haven't had one in ten thousand years. I wonder if my body still remembers how to react. You mortals have immune systems that learn, right? Well, mine has had ten millennia to evolve without any real work. Let's give it a test."

I couldn't reply. I just watched the enemy.

They called it the God-Severing Singularity. It was less a weapon and more a final, desperate thesis: every multiverse in creation contributed its ultimate power source, every dead god donated its last spark, every philosopher-warrior fed their concept of "victory" into a single point. If you could quantify it, it was the combined might of infinity squared. They had taken all the omnipotent entities that were not Godric, duplicated them across recursive temporal loops, and then merged them into a spear that existed in every dimension, past, present, and future, all targeting one specific location—the exact centre of Godric's chest.

They had been preparing for millennia, their greatest minds devising stratagems that, they thought, were unknown to us. But Godric knew. He knew when they formed the first thought of rebellion. He could have stopped them with a whim. He let them grow, let them feed his weakness paradox with every plan, every contingency, every fleeting fantasy of his downfall. They had no idea that the very act of scheming made him infinitely more powerful.

And now, here they were.

I saw their generals give the signal—a ripple of light that transcended language. The spear ignited. It didn't travel; it simply manifested in contact with the skin-cell barrier. Reality screamed.

Now, if I were a chronicler who craved a tidy narrative, I would tell you that the weapon struck and, against all cosmic odds, a hairline crack appeared. I would describe the silence that followed, the sharp intake of breath across a trillion worlds, the first tears of disbelieving joy. I would paint the scene of the Coalition's collective consciousness erupting in euphoria, weapons dropped, voices lifted in a victory chant that shook the stars. They'd embrace, these mortal and immortal beings who had sacrificed everything, and they'd think, *He bleeds. He is not absolute.*

But that story is a lie.

That celebration never happened. The crack did appear—Godric willed it exactly as the spear touched—but before a single neuron could fire in a single rebel's brain, before the first fragment of hope could crystallize, his immune system had already responded. In the span of zero seconds, a cascade of absurd overkill was triggered that not only reversed the "injury" but annihilated the entire omniverse. And the rebels never even knew they'd been erased. Their moment of triumph was a stillborn thing, suffocated by the body of a god that treats a cracked dead skin cell as a capital offense.

I saw it happen—or rather, I perceived it in the way a mortal brain can perceive an event that occurs outside of time. The crack formed. And instantly, the dead skin cell changed. It didn't simply heal. It evolved. The flake of keratin underwent a phase-shift into a self-aware material that defied all physics: a living void of absolute negation. It expanded, not outward but inward-outward, severing the causal link between the weapon and reality. The spear, that conflux of infinite power, was un-made so thoroughly that it retroactively ceased to exist across all timelines, and the concept of its existence was deleted from memory. The rebels holding it had time to register one microsecond of confusion before the void turned its attention to them.

But that was just the mildest reaction.

Godric's bloodstream, an ocean of liquid fire that could dissolve omniverses, deployed a fleet of conceptual antibodies. Each was a self-contained universe designed to hunt a single target. They traced the lines of intent: every strategist who plotted, every smith who forged the spear's components, every foot-soldier who lent their psionic energy. The antibodies descended not on their physical forms but on their "existence templates"—the fundamental blueprint that said a being was real. In an eternal instant, those templates were shredded. I saw a rebel general, a seven-dimensional entity of pure thought, convulse as his very "I" was methodically peeled back layer by layer: first his identity, then his memories, then his ability to perceive time, then his acknowledgment of self. He was turned inside out, his consciousness pinned to a singularity of agony that stretched his final moment into a perceived infinity. And then he was nothing, never having been.

Across the Coalition, identical fates unfolded. Beings of living fire were reduced to numb, screaming flesh. Creatures that had existed since before light were regressed to primordial plasma, then to less than plasma, held at the threshold of existence just long enough to experience the horror of non-being before being wiped. The antibodies were thorough: they didn't just kill; they unmade families, lineages, entire species, all of time that touched the target. And they did this to every single participant, simultaneously.

I was dimly aware of Godric's voice beside me, conversational in tone. "Ah, yes, there's the backup verification. Watch this, Leon. It's rather amusing."

What I saw next didn't amuse me; it broke something fundamental in my mind. Godric, I knew, existed in infinite identical copies across infinite realities—a redundancy so vast that it couldn't be called immortality because the word was too small. For an injury to be considered real, every single copy, across every layer of the infinite recursion (each copy themselves possessing infinite copies), must experience the exact same crack at the exact same instant. This is a physical impossibility, a paradox that not even the omniverse's most deranged logics can satisfy. Yet his immune system, possessively paranoid, assumes the worst. It detected a single scratch on one copy—the copy standing beside me—and screamed to all others that a breach had occurred. Instantly, every Godric across infinity entered a synchronized evolution. Their biologies, already beyond any notion of perfection, cross-communicated and merged. The skin cells of one copy shared their new adaptive data with all, and the collective set of defenses was upgraded across the board. It was as if a single man stubbed his toe, and suddenly the entire multiverse of men gained bulletproof skin, all because the immune system couldn't tolerate even the idea that a toe could be stubbed.

I felt it more than saw it: a wave of absolute invulnerability cascading through reality, making Godric not just immune to the spear, but immune to the category of action that the spear represented. The concept of "weapon" itself was rendered inert across the entire omniverse. Anything designed to harm another living thing ceased to function. Swords shattered in sheaths, guns turned to sand, claws retracted, fangs dulled. The antibodies had pre-emptively pacified existence, just in case. And this was still, I realized, a child's version of his body's true power—the gentlest of his automatic defenses.

And then the weakness paradox kicked in. The omniverse witnessed the "harm"—even though it was staged, even though it was self-willed—and its own self-regulating mechanisms panicked. By its law, Godric can never have a weakness. The mere perception of one made it overcompensate. It flooded him with a new tier of authority, a cosmic apology that elevated his already trans-infinite amplification rate by another infinite exponentiation. He was now even more untouchable than he had been a moment ago, which was already infinity. The gap between him and the rest of existence, already an insurmountable infinity, became an infinity of infinities. And all of this happened because he had humored the idea of a scratch.

The entire Coalition was long gone by then—unmade, purged, their histories erased. They had been, in the truest sense, undone. I stared at the void where they had been, my body shaking so violently my teeth clattered.

Godric exhaled, a sound of mild disappointment. "They didn't even make it through the first response layer. I was hoping for at least a shiver." He turned to me, his expression that of a chef whose soufflé had not risen. "I think my immune system overreacted. It's always so literal. I told it to heal a scratch, and it decided to sterilize the entire Petri dish."

He then did something that made my soul attempt to flee my body.

"I suppose I should put it back," he said, and he did.

With no gesture, no incantation, no perceivable effort, the entire omniverse was restored. Every star, every galaxy, every plane of existence that had been annihilated reappeared. It was not a rewind of time; it was a complete recreation from nothing, executed in zero seconds. The Coalition members blinked into existence, their weapons in hand, their minds exactly where they were before the attack—except all memory of the "crack" and the subsequent annihilation was absent. They were primed to strike, yet hesitating, because something felt off. I could see the confusion on their faces—that deep, psychic unease that comes from being resurrected without consent.

Godric waved a hand through the barrier, and the skin-cell wall shimmered back to pristine. He spoke to his own body: "There, you see? It's all better. No harm done. You really must learn restraint." Then, to me, with a warm, friendly grin: "Leon, I think I'll have to teach my immune system how to hold back. It's completely clueless about proportional response."

I laughed. It was not a sober laugh, but the cracked sound of a man whose mind has visited the abyss and returned without a souvenir. "Your Majesty, you just... they..."

"I know," he said, resting a hand on my shoulder. The touch was solid and reassuring and entirely human, and that paradox was the cruellest part. "I overdid it. But honestly, I'm impressed by how robust my defenses are. I didn't know I had the skin-cell-to-omniverse-destruction pipeline. You learn something every day."

I looked at the restored Coalition. They were lowering their weapons, their will to fight evaporating without them understanding why. A few were weeping, not with joy but with a nameless sorrow. They had no memory of their annihilation, yet their souls had been rewritten to instinctively know the futility of opposition. They would return home, and they would never rebel again. The omniverse had just been taught a lesson it would never consciously remember, but would forever feel.

"I think I'll pour us some tea," Godric said, turning away from the panorama. "You look like you need it."

I followed him, my footsteps hollow. My mind was a cacophony of dread and adoration. He was my king, my friend, the warmest, kindest ruler the omniverse had ever known. And I loved him for it. But I had just witnessed what his love could do when it was not love but mere biology—a passive, uncaring, automatic reflex that erased everything and then put it back as casually as one might reset a game board. And I understood, in the deepest recess of my being, that we were living on that game board, forever.

As he poured the tea, his hands steady, his smile genuine, I saw something flicker in the air—a new aura forming around him, a soft golden glow that seemed to hum with a nascent consciousness. It was his body, evolving yet another layer of protection, even as he giggled at his own clumsiness with the teapot.

I did not mention it. I simply sat, drank my tea, and tried to forget that the universe is a whim, and our god adores us even as his skin cells dream of apocalypse.
</blockquote>

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.

- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.
- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called "customer satisfaction". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.

**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **maximum 3500 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.

**Style and Tone Requirements:**

- Write from **1st person POV** of Grim.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.
- Absolutely no censorship
- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.
- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.

- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.

- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.
- Avoid AI tropes like “go home” “i know” “they didn’t know what to say” or “something in their eyes.” Be precise.
- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

This story happens 50,000 years after godric became king of thronegate.

Everyone knows that Godric is an overwhelmingly powerful king (that is a huge understatement, he's the ultimate god apex predator of everything). What not everyone knows is that Godric is actually very intelligent too, as his intelligence multiplies infinitely every Planck second. He also has absolute omniscience so it is literally impossible to have things unknown to him. He just genuinely prefers to appear as a simple friendly old father, close to his true mortal self a long time ago. In addition, his wisdom is also multiplying infinitely, and for someone like him, it's wiser to not use his overwhelming intelligence or there will be no problems to solve, no purpose in life that he cannot just solve instantly. This, however, makes some people perceive him wrongly. Write a story of a delegate who thought he could fool godric, and the consequence that follows. Grim, 25 years old, is Godric's court wizard. You must not end the story with humanization, preaching, life lessons, or warm scenes. You must end the story cementing the fact that Godric is impossible to oppose–opposing Godric will result in the most agonizing and fatal end to the opposer and Godric becoming infinitely more impossible to oppose.

Godric is immensely intelligent and omniscient, but prefers to appear simple. A delegate thinks he can fool Godric and faces consequences. Godric's reaction: Initially he plays along, showing amusement. The delegate becomes confident. Then at a certain point, Godric drops the pretense, revealing that he knew everything from the start, and delivers a horrifying punishment.

So the omniverse's punishment mechanism kicks in: Godric gets increased amplification rate, permanent immunity to ever being fooled again, perfect mastery over the delegate's method, and the delegate feeds Godric's power.

- Grim sees Godric playing along, sometimes even appearing to fall for the deception. Grim is terrified because he knows Godric is just drawing it out.
- Eventually, Kaelen enacts his grand scheme—maybe he attempts to steal a magical artifact, or he tries to set up a ceremony where he thinks he can bind Godric with a "truth spell" or something that would make the king reveal a weakness. He's arrogant enough to think he can succeed.
- Godric drops the act. In a terrifying scene, he reveals that he knew every thought from the beginning. He then subjects Kaelen to a fate worse than death: perhaps he "unweaves" him, making him experience all possible agonies simultaneously, or he makes him a living statue, or uses his perfect mastery of Kaelen's strategies to turn them against him and his entire lineage, erasing them from existence retroactively.
- The Weakness Paradox triggers, and Grim sees the air shimmer as Godric's power elevates further. Godric comments that he always appreciates a good laugh, but no one has ever truly fooled him, and now his wisdom has grown yet again.
- The delegate's home universe is probably punished as well, perhaps erased or reduced to a husk.
- Grim concludes that Godric is the apex, and the thought of ever opposing him is absurd, because the very act of thinking you could win only makes him stronger. The story ends with a chilling note.

- No warm ending, no humanization.

He believes Godric is a beast with unlimited power but no real intellect, and that he can be intellectually subjugated. He looks directly into Kaelen's eyes and says that the token is a psionic dampener, and he's known since before it was forged. He describes every step of Kaelen's plan in excruciating detail, including how Kaelen murdered his own wife to take credit for the artifact. Then the horror begins.
6. Godric decides to punish him not just for the deception but for the arrogance. He invokes a punishment that I need to imagine. It should be extremely graphic, painful, and demonstrate his cruelty. For example: "I will give you what you wanted, Kaelen. You wished to witness my intelligence. So I will show you the full scope of what your tiny mind attempted to manipulate." He then forces Kaelen's consciousness to experience the infinite multivariate calculations happening in Godric's mind for a single Planck second. His brain overloads, his body begins to atomize, but Godric keeps him alive and conscious through it, unmaking each atom in sequence while he screams. Or perhaps Godric uses his perfect mastery to deny Kaelen death, keeping him in an eternal loop of torment.
7. The Weakness Paradox: As Kaelen suffers, Godric remarks that even the thought that Godric could be outsmarted triggered an upgrade. He can never be deceived again—not that he ever could—and he's now immune to all forms of cognition manipulation on an omniversal scale. The rate of his stat multiplication skyrockets.
8. The aftermath: Kaelen is erased from existence, his homeworld's sun is extinguished, and the people there are left in darkness as a reminder. The rest of the delegation is spared but traumatized.
9. Grim's closing thoughts: The apex predator, the mathematical impossibility, the tragedy of opposing him. End with a cold, dread-inducing line.

Grim knows better. He tries to warn Kaelen indirectly, but Kaelen dismisses it.

With a thought, Godric transmits a sliver of his ongoing mental computations into Kaelen's mind—not all of it, just a fragment. The fragment instantly overloads Kaelen's neural capacity, causing his brain to hemorrhage. But Godric keeps him conscious, extending the moment into a subjective eternity of agony. He makes Kaelen experience the recursive nature of his omniscience: knowing that he knows that he knows, ad infinitum. I'll write the story now.

This story takes place 80,000 years after Godric becomes the King of Thronegate. Throughout the years, Blake's descendants have served Godric as court wizard. Godric never actually needs their magical protection, healing, help, or anything that a typical court wizard typically provides. Godric’s court wizard’s magics are really potent and terrifying, especially since all of them receive a thousandfold daily amplification from the awakening after they age 20 (which is a gift from Godric himself, but they don't know. Note for you: the thousandfold daily amplification is not to protect Blake or his descendants from Godric--as established in previous lore, Godric has absolute concealment which allows him to appear as normal human so he has no leaked aura or presence at all if he wish to.), but compared to Godric whose all magical traits are multiplying infinitely every Planck second, they are laughable, pretty much 0 (not to mention Godric could instantly and  effortlessly delete the very concept of magic from ever existing, which he didn't do because wizard needs magic and his best friends are wizards. The story will shatter that belief. Must exaggerate Godric's magical aptitude horrifically: an infinitesimal fraction (practically 0% of his magic) can erase entire omniverse infinite times over instantly and effortlessly. So Godric's magic is beyond infinite. Gorm's magic is extremely powerful but compared to Godric's it's zero.

Maybe a powerful enemy, a magical catastrophe, a natural cosmic horror, or a rebellious mage. Gorm prepares to defend Godric with all his magical might, but Godric casually, instantly, effortlessly prevents the threat with an almost imperceptible application of his own magic, and even that is an infinitesimal fraction of his power. Gorm's mind breaks from the realization. The aftermath: Gorm's worldview shattered, he can't see Godric the same way; the dread of knowing that his own magic, his whole lineage's purpose, is laughably irrelevant. Yet he must continue to serve as court wizard because that's tradition and because Godric values him as a friend. But the existential horror lingers. The ending must cement the impossibility of opposing Godric: maybe the enemy is utterly obliterated in a gruesome, agonizing manner, and Godric becomes even more powerful (weakness paradox triggered subtly? No need, but show that opposition simply feeds his ascendancy).

We need to include extreme violence/gore in the enemy's demise. Possibly the enemy is another universe's ultimate wizard or god who challenges Godric, thinking they can defeat him. Gorm initially thinks he must protect Godric; he steps forward, but Godric stops him with a friendly gesture, then demonstrates his own power. The horror should be from Gorm's POV, describing the scale and ease.

Structure: 1st person POV of Gorm. Begin with his perspective, his relationship with Godric, his training as court wizard, his pride in his magic. Then the inciting event: a threat appears. He readies his magic. Godric dismisses it casually, then unleashes something—maybe just a fraction of a thought—that annihilates the threat in a way that reveals his infinite magical mastery. Gorm's inner turmoil and realization. Then the aftermath: maybe Godric acts as if nothing happened, uncle-ly affection, but Gorm can't shake the dread. No warm ending; end with a sense of doom, acknowledging that Godric cannot be opposed, and Gorm's own role is a futile tradition.

Word count: max 3500 words. We'll aim for around 3000-3500.

Key details: Godric's magical aptitude: should say his magic is such that an infinitesimal sliver (practically 0% of his true magic) could erase the entire omniverse infinite times over. This is the kind of exaggeration we need. And he can delete the concept of magic, but he doesn't because his friends are wizards, and they need magic. So he holds back.

The Awakening: Gorm's daily amplification is 1000x per day past age 20. He just turned 20, so maybe he's just starting to feel the amplification. He hasn't yet realized the true scale of Godric's power because Godric conceals it.

We must include the weakness paradox? Not needed explicitly, but can be if it fits. However, the prompt doesn't mention it; it's about Godric's magical aptitude. So we focus on that.

We need to include that Godric's all stats multiply infinitely every Planck second, including his magical power, wisdom, intelligence. So his magic is also multiplying at that rate.

Plan: Gorm, age 20, has just completed his initial training as court wizard. He has immense magical power from his lineage plus the Awakening (which he doesn't know is from Godric). He's eager to prove himself. He accompanies Godric to a diplomatic meeting with a realm that believes magic is supreme and challenges Godric's authority. The realm's archmage, the most powerful magic-user in that universe, demands to face Thronegate's champion in a magic duel to prove superiority. Gorm immediately volunteers, but Godric gently declines, saying he'll handle it. Gorm argues that the king shouldn't risk himself, and he insists that his magic is more than enough. Godric, with a knowing smile, says, "You've never seen what I can do, Gorm. I keep it hidden because it's not needed." Then he proceeds to demonstrate. He doesn't even cast a spell; he just thinks, and the entire realm's magic is nullified, the archmage is reduced to a screaming pile of flesh in a fraction of a second, his magical essence extracted and used to fuel a eternal torment. Godric then explains that his magical aptitude is beyond infinite, that even holding back 99.999...% still results in absurd power. He reveals to Gorm (and the reader) that his court wizard's role is not for protection but for companionship and tradition. Gorm's entire identity collapses.

Aftermath: Gorm is in shock; he can't reconcile the friendly uncle with this cosmic horror. He continues to serve because he has no choice, but now every time he performs a spell, he feels utterly useless and terrified. The ending should emphasize that any opposition to Godric is futile, and Godric becomes stronger from it.

We must avoid humanization and warm scenes at the end. End with dread.

Let's flesh out the scene.

**Title**: I'll keep it as no title needed; just story.

**First-person POV**: Gorm's voice. He's 20 years old, newly appointed as court wizard. He's enthusiastic, idealistic. He's known Godric all his life, called him "Uncle Godric" as a child. He's proud of his magic, which is already formidable. He senses the king has no magical aura, so he assumes Godric is a mundane in that respect. He believes the kings have kept court wizards for generations because they lack magical talent. He doesn't know about the Stasis event or Godric's powers beyond the general reputation of his godlike supremacy but thinks it's more of a physical/mental amplification, not magic. Because Godric never uses magic overtly.

Now, the inciting event: a delegation from the "Sorcerer-Kingdom of Zyrak" where magic is the measure of worth. They refuse to bow to a "magically void brute" (as they perceive Godric). They demand a magical duel. Gorm jumps in, eager to defend. He challenges their champion. Godric gently places a hand on his shoulder. "Let me, Gorm. It's been a long time since anyone needed reminding." Gorm protests, saying his magic can handle it. Godric laughs softly, then says, "Watch."

What follows: Godric doesn't move, doesn't even gesture. The air doesn't change, but suddenly the Zyrak champion—a thousand-year-old lich with countless artifacts—screams. His body is turned inside out without any visible cause. The soul is extracted, shaped into a small gem, and dropped into Godric's palm. Then Godric addresses the Zyrak people: "You think magic is power. I could unmake the concept entirely. But I won't, because my friends are wizards and I'd miss their company." With a thought, he eradicates every magical ward, artifact, and spell in the entire universe of Zyrak, leaving them all magically null. The people fall in terror. Gorm, watching, feels his own magic—which he thought was immense—flicker in existential horror. He realizes that his entire magic is less than a drop compared to the ocean of Godric's. In fact, Godric's passive presence, completely held back, still made Gorm's magic feel like a candle before the sun. And that was Godric holding back nearly everything. He then understands that Godric's court wizards are there for companionship, not protection. The line of Blake served as friends, not magical protectors.

The aftermath: Gorm is shattered. He tries to reconcile the warm uncle who taught him to fish with this entity. He can't. He continues to serve because it's all he knows, but every spell he casts feels hollow. The existential dread: if Godric wanted, he could delete magic itself, and Gorm would become a normal human. And there's nothing he could do. The realization that all his training, his bloodline, his destiny, is insignificant. But he still serves, because opposing Godric is not possible—and attempting to do so only feeds Godric's infinite growth.

We must end with a note that Godric's power is even greater now because the Zyrak people's attempt (thinking magic could oppose him) triggered the weakness paradox? Not necessary, but we can hint that any opposition only makes him more absolute.

Now, incorporate the "infinitesimal fraction" description. For example, after the display, Godric tells Gorm that what he just used was 0.000... (infinite zeroes) 1% of his true capacity, and even that was an exaggeration. He could erase the entire omniverse a trillion times over with the magical equivalent of a stray thought. That's the absurd scale.

Also, we need to show Gorm's magical aptitude. He has 1000x daily multiplication, so at 20, he's only just beginning to amplify. But his bloodline already has potent magic. However, compared to Godric's Planck-second infinite multiplication, it's nothing.

We should use the fact that Godric's magical traits multiply infinitely every Planck second, not just his stats. So his magic is not static; it's growing at an incomprehensible rate. The magic he used today is infinitely more powerful than the magic he would have used a second ago. So even if Gorm somehow could match a version of Godric from a Planck second ago, he'd still be infinitely outmatched now.

We can incorporate that by having Gorm sense, through his connection to magic, that Godric's magical power is increasing continuously, and he realizes the implication.

Now, write the story in a raw, oppressive style, focusing on sensory details and internal dread.

Let's outline:

1. Gorm's POV: Introduction of his role, his relationship with Godric, his pride in his magic, his misinterpretation.
2. The Zyrak delegation arrives, making demands. Their champion, Azarak, a powerful sorcerer. Gorm steps forward to challenge, but Godric stops him.
3. Godric's demonstration: calmly nullifies Azarak's spells, inflicts horrific and slow destruction, amplifies the horror. Use extreme gore: flesh boiling, bones snapping, eyes melting, consciousness trapped in a loop of agony. Then erasure of the entire universe's magic, not killing but leaving them helpless.
4. Godric's explanation to Gorm: He's always had magic beyond comprehension. He concealed it because it's not needed and because he likes the company of wizards. He reveals the scale: his magic is a bottomless abyss; what Gorm saw was him holding back so much that it was practically a nonexistent fraction.
5. Gorm's internal crisis: He looks at his own hands, feels his magic, and it seems laughable. He remembers all the times he'd offered to protect Godric, and the king's gentle smile. He now understands the smile was not indulgence but pity.
6. Aftermath: Gorm continues his duties, but the joy is gone. He feels a constant, gnawing dread. He cannot look at Godric the same way. The story ends with a reflection that no one can oppose Godric, and that the very concept of magic depends on his whim. Any attempt to use magic against him would be futile, and the mere thought would make him even more invulnerable. The closing lines should cement the terror.

Avoid life lessons, warm scenes. End with a bleak, oppressive tone.

Now write the story. Use maximum word count allowed. Include descriptions that exaggerate the horror.

Be careful to follow: Godric "possesses absolute omniscience and absolute concealment." So Godric knows everything Gorm thinks. Thus, during the conversation, Godric could subtly hint that he knows Gorm's beliefs. That adds to the dread. Godric might even say, "You always thought I needed protection, didn't you?" with a gentle, fatherly tone. That's chilling.

Also, note that Godric's absolute concealment allows him to appear as normal. So Gorm never sensed any magic from him. But now, after the event, Gorm could perceive something—maybe a flicker—or his magic can never sense Godric's, which is even more terrifying.

I plan to include the line: "An infinitesimal fraction—a sliver so small that it would take a mathematician a billion lifetimes to write the number of zeros after the decimal point—of Godric's true magical might could unravel every reality, invert causality, and extinguish the omniverse so many times over that the number of extinctions would become a new infinity, and that infinity would be recursively extinguished, and still the fraction would remain undiminished." Something like that.

Now let's write the story.

The conquered do not get Awakening.\n\n**Part 6: The Futility of Resistance** \u2013 An external powerful entity thinks Godric has a weakness. Elaborate on their plan. Show that the moment they thought it, Godric's power increased, and he became immune. The entity proceeds with their attack, only to realize they were doomed from the start. Godric may not even notice, or he toys with them. The entity experiences absolute despair. Show the defense mechanism in action.\n\n**Part 7: Character Dynamics and Conclusion** \u2013 Godric's bond with Blake. Blake influences Godric to become warm and kind again, but still ruthless to enemies. Blake transitions from merchant to court wizard. Hint his son Josh will follow. Final scene: present-day Thronegate, Godric ruling, Blake at his side. Show the peace and prosperity, but undercurrent of absolute power.\n\nWe must ensure Godric's omniscience is evident throughout. He knows everything. So in his dialogue or actions, he can reference things he shouldn't know. Also, the weakness paradox: show that even a stray thought triggers it. So in the attempted exploitation, the entity might be planning, and Godric might speak to them, revealing he already knows their plan and that their very thought made him more powerful. That's terrifying.\n\nGiven the word limit, I'll write concisely but with intense detail. I'll use lengthy sentences and paragraphs to convey the epic scale. I'll avoid bullet points entirely. I'll use line breaks between sections but no headers? The prompt says \"prose paragraphs only\" but we can structure with section breaks as long as they are not bullet points. I'll just write a continuous narrative with implied sections.\n\nLet's begin drafting.\n\nWe must incorporate the amplification mechanic details: stats multiply by 1000 and by itself every Planck second. That's an incomprehensible rate. We need to convey that without getting too technical. Use descriptions like \"each infinitesimal fragment of time doubled his might beyond the previous infinity\" etc.\n\nThe concealment power: he holds back his aura, but when he releases even a fraction, it's overwhelming.\n\nNow, for the battle, we need to show the army's confidence and then the horror. Godric must not move a muscle. He could use telekinesis, reality warping, or simply think them out of existence. I'll have him stand still, perhaps with a slight smile, and the army is dismantled by their own weapons turning on them, or by sudden mutations, or by a plague of madness. But make it visceral: limbs tearing, dragons imploding, ninjas aging rapidly. Show the soldiers' terror through their thoughts and actions.\n\nFor the subjugation examples, I'll do one where Godric destroys a universe because he was annoyed by its existence (maybe he found its music irritating), and it vanishes in a fraction of a second. Another where a squad of five older Thronegate men conquer a highly advanced universe that prepared for years, and they do it in under 30 minutes with ease, but they are apologetic. A third where the universe surrenders immediately, but we can also show a universe that didn't surrender and was crushed.\n\nFor the attempted exploitation, I'll create a being from outside the omniverse, perhaps a conceptual entity, who thinks Godric's weakness is his love for Blake or his past trauma. They plan to attack Blake or use time manipulation to prevent the stasis. But the moment they conceive the idea, Godric's defense triggers. As they enact their plan, Godric reveals that they only exist because he allows it, and their attempt has only made him stronger. Their despair is absolute.\n\nNow, I need to seed hints that Blake is Thorin's descendant. For example, Blake might have a ring with Thorin's family crest, or a natural affinity for magic, or the sanctuary only opened for him because of his bloodline. But never explicitly state it. Also, Blake's rapid learning of wizardry later could be a hint.\n\nI'll write the story in a single narrative flow, starting with Olympus, then the future, then the battle, etc. I'll use Godric's point of view at times, but mostly third-person limited to various characters to show the dread.\n\nLet's start writing.\n\n**The Fall of Olympus**\n\nThe morning of Isabel's wedding, the air over Olympus tasted of honey and roasted lamb. Godric stood at the great hall's threshold, his silhouette a monument of muscle and calm. At forty-five, he still moved with the coiled grace of a predator, though his touch was gentle when he cupped his wife Reina's chin. \"She will be happy,\" he murmured, his deep voice carrying the warmth of a hearth. Reina leaned into his chest, her silver-threaded hair catching the light. Their daughters, Isabel and young Hebe, giggled beyond the colonnade, wreaths of white blossoms in their hair.\n\nThe ceremony began in the palace courtyard. Thorin, the court wizard, adjusted his cobalt robes beside the altar, his family's ancient grimoire resting open. He caught Godric's eye and grinned, a familiar, easy expression born of decades of friendship. \"You've rehearsed the blessing, I trust?\" Godric teased. Thorin snorted. \"I could speak it in my sleep.\"\n\nThen the sky turned to black iron. The first volley of Thronegate's siege engines struck the eastern parapets before the bells could toll. Fire and stone vomited into the courtyard. A shard of obsidian masonry sheared through the wedding canopy. Godric threw himself over Reina, but the second impact lifted them both and hurled them into a crumbling fountain. He surfaced from the water in time to see Isabel\u2019s white gown darkening with red, her body pinned beneath a fallen column. Hebe\u2019s small hand twitched once under a drift of ash, then stilled. Reina\u2019s eyes, still open, reflected the conflagration before the light fled them.\n\nA howl\u2014more vibration than sound\u2014tore from Godric\u2019s chest. He crawled through the carnage, muscles tearing as he tried to reach his daughters. Thorin appeared, bleeding from a gash across his scalp, and seized Godric\u2019s arm. \"There\u2019s a spell\u2014my ancestors\u2014it will send you somewhere safe. I can\u2019t save them, but I can save you!\" He began to chant, the words clawing at reality, bending the air into fractals. A Thronegate assassin\u2019s blade sprouted from Thorin\u2019s throat before the final syllable. The wizard collapsed, his dying gasp misting the grimoire\u2019s pages.\n\nThe incomplete spell caught Godric mid-scream. The world folded. He felt himself wrenched sideways through a membrane of cold nothingness, and then he was in a dark, echoing sanctuary, lined with obsidian and cobwebs. A deep stasis gripped him, his limbs freezing mid-motion, his roar trapped in his lungs. But his mind did not sleep.\n\nIn that frozen instant, his body ceased to age. The need for air, for food, for rest\u2014all vanished. And then the first multiplication came: a subtle, internal lurch as his strength doubled, then quadrupled, then exploded into a thousandfold, and that thousandfold multiplied by itself in the following Planck second. His endurance, his speed, his wisdom, his senses\u2014each stat became a recursive singularity of increase. At the same moment, a new power blossomed within him: the ability to unmake matter with a thought. And before the thought could fully form, that power, too, began amplifying at the same infinite rate. Another power came: perfect concealment, a veil that could hold back the tidal wave of his presence from obliterating the cosmos. And another, and another, one per second, each apocalyptic on its birth, each compounding into impossibility.\n\nBut the most insidious defense activated simultaneously. As his body lay in stasis, the universe etched a new law into his being: Godric had no weaknesses. Any sentient mind that even imagined he did\u2014any nascent speculation of an exploit\u2014would instantly and permanently accelerate his amplification, grant him total immunity to the conceived attack, and bestow upon him perfect mastery over it. The thought alone would feed him. The plan would damn the planner. And he would know, with absolute omniscience, every whisper of defiance across the omniverse.\n\nTen thousand years passed. Olympus became dust, forgotten by history. Thronegate rose from a marauding kingdom into the galaxy\u2019s supreme power, its armies fuelled by sorcery and industry. And in a forgotten ruin on a backwater world, a merchant named Blake stumbled upon a hidden door.\n\nBlake was thirty-eight, his mutton chops flecked with grey, his temper quick but his heart honest. He\u2019d been searching for salvageable tech to pay off a debt when his foot broke through a rotten floor into a subterranean chamber. Anna would scold him for the risk, but the anomaly on his handheld scanner promised profit. He found a crystalline pod at the room\u2019s centre, and inside it, a man.\n\nThe man\u2019s eyes opened before the pod cracked. A low, resonant hum filled the space, and Blake staggered back as the crystal dissolved. Godric stepped out, his appearance exactly as it had been ten millennia ago\u2014forty-five, magnificent, salt-and-pepper beard neat, chiselled features placid. But the air around him felt like the pressure before a storm you couldn\u2019t comprehend.\n\n\"You are Blake,\" Godric said. It wasn\u2019t a question. His voice vibrated in Blake\u2019s bones. \"Descendant of Thorin\u2019s line, though you do not know it.\" Blake\u2019s throat tightened. \"I\u2026 I don\u2019t know what you\u2019re talking about. I\u2019m just a merchant.\" Godric tilted his head, a faint, almost fond smile touching his lips. \"You released me. That debt I will honour.\" Then his gaze shifted, as if looking through the planet\u2019s crust into the galaxy beyond. \"Thronegate has prospered, I see. Their king is a boy named Robert. He will abdicate, or I will erase his army.\"\n\nBlake blinked, his temper flaring despite his fear. \"Now hold on\u2014you can\u2019t just\u2014\". Godric laid a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and the contact felt like being grounded during an electrical surge. \"I mean them no lasting harm, if they are wise. But I have waited an eternity. Three days. That is what I will give them.\"\n\nThe next seventy-two hours passed in a blur for Blake. Godric used no vehicle; he simply folded space and brought Blake and his family to a high ridge overlooking Thronegate\u2019s capital. Anna clutched Josh and Rhea, her knuckles white. \"Who is this man, Blake?\" she whispered. He could only shake his head.\n\nOn the third day, the Thronegate host assembled. They stretched from horizon to horizon\u2014billions of super-soldiers in power armour that hummed with the energy of captive suns. Mage battalions levitated in geometric formations, their staves crackling with spells that could unravel time. Robotic leviathans the size of mountains rumbled forward, their cannons loaded with singularity warheads. Dragons with scales harder than neutronium darkened the sky, and among the ranks, squads of ninjas flickered, their movements so swift they created localized time loops, already perceiving the battle as won.\n\nKing Robert, a slim young man with a golden circlet, strode before his troops and raised a sceptre. \"Stranger, you have threatened my crown. Behold the might of Thronegate. Surrender, and I may grant you a swift death.\"\n\nGodric stood a hundred metres ahead, alone on the plain, still in the simple tunic and trousers Blake had given him. He hadn\u2019t moved a muscle. He didn\u2019t need to.\n\nThe first wave of soldiers charged. Half a billion enhanced warriors, each capable of leveling a city, surged forward. Godric\u2019s lips didn\u2019t move. A thought\u2014not even a focused one, more an idle recognition of their existence\u2014rippled outward. The front line didn\u2019t just die; they came apart. Armour and flesh and bone separated into their constituent particles, then recombined into a fine mist that drifted back over the second line. The mist carried the scent of copper and ozone. The second line of soldiers inhaled it, and their own bodies began to dissolve from the inside, arteries and organs liquefying. They opened their mouths to scream, but only pink froth emerged before their forms collapsed into wet heaps.\n\nThe mages retaliated, weaving a combined spell designed to erase Godric from the timeline. Reality shimmered, causal threads snapping. Godric simply remained. He allowed the temporal paradox to wash over him, and then, with a glance at the mages, he reversed it. The spell backlashed, and the mages aged ten billion years in a heartbeat. Their bodies desiccated, skeletons crumbling to fine powder that got lost in the breeze.\n\nThe robots fired their singularity warheads. The projectiles, each a miniature black hole, crossed the distance in a nanosecond. They stopped an inch from Godric\u2019s skin, then turned around. The black holes expanded to swallow the robotic legions, compressing them into singularities so dense that light itself spiralled into them. The ground shook as the war machines vanished with a sound like tearing silk.\n\nThe dragons dove, breathing plasma that could vaporize continents. Godric\u2019s gaze met the lead dragon\u2019s. The beast\u2019s mind, ancient and proud, shattered into a million fragments. It turned on its brethren, tearing wings with its fangs, igniting a chain of fiery cannibalism in the sky. Charred dragonflesh rained onto the army below, starting panicked fires.\n\nThe time ninjas attempted their ultimate technique, accelerating to reverse causality itself, aiming to kill Godric before he had woken. But the moment they slipped out of the timestream, they found him already there, waiting in the void between seconds\u2014except he was a billion times larger, his form an impossible geometry of endless eyes and teeth. Their minds broke. They returned to the present as drooling, catatonic husks.\n\nThrough it all, Godric did not shift his weight. His hands remained at his sides. On the ridge, Blake watched with his family, and he felt a terror so profound it bypassed his brain and settled into his marrow. Anna sobbed silently. Rhea buried her face in her father\u2019s chest. Josh, though, stared with wide, unblinking eyes, as if trying to understand.\n\nKing Robert saw annihilation and fled back to his palace. Two days later, his servants found him hanging from his throne room\u2019s chandelier. Godric walked through the capital\u2019s gates, and the surviving population knelt. He seated himself on the throne and issued the Decree of Awakening.\n\nEvery Thronegate man, from the moment they turned twenty, would find their strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom multiplied tenfold for each day lived past that age. This applied retroactively. Men who were forty became demigods overnight. They could dial their power down to a whisper or let it roar. They still aged, dying around eighty, but those final years were of terrifying potency. Women received no such enhancement, but Godric decreed them sacrosanct\u2014no man under his rule could harm a woman without facing his direct, creative punishment.\n\nBlake, for reasons no one explained, received a modified Awakening. His increases were a thousandfold per day. He felt it in the mornings: a deepening reservoir of perception and vigour that frightened him as much as it thrilled him. He used it to protect his family and, eventually, to stand at Godric\u2019s side.\n\nUnder Godric, Thronegate looked outward. There were other universes, teeming with civilizations that had never heard of Olympus or Thronegate. Godric sent offers of unconditional surrender. Some refused.\n\nUniverse 77-B was a realm of crystal beings whose thoughts manipulated dark matter. They had watched the edges of their cosmos tremble and spent five years building defences: planet-sized cannons that fired causality disruptions, star forts that could shift dimensions. When the Thronegate squad arrived\u2014five men, the youngest thirty-eight, the oldest seventy-four\u2014the crystal beings activated their weapons. The squad leader, a farmer named Darian, sighed and told his companions, \"Let\u2019s make it quick. The king dislikes delays.\" In eighteen minutes, the crystal armies were shattered, their star forts imploded, their dimension-shifters trapped in pocket spaces of their own making. Darian personally ripped the core from their war-moon with his bare hands, then wept quietly afterward because the destruction reminded him of a harvest gone wrong. The conquered universe was folded into the protectorate, its people allowed to live, but denied the Awakening. They would never rise.\n\nAnother universe, designation 9-Alpha, was a hyper-intelligent hivemind of fungal spores. They refused surrender by sending a cloud of corrosive memes toward Thronegate\u2019s emissaries. Godric, in his palace, wrinkled his nose. \"That aroma,\" he murmured to Blake, \"it\u2019s reminiscent of the rot in Olympus\u2019s courtyard.\" He didn\u2019t stand, didn\u2019t gesture. He merely thought: *Cleanse it*. Universe 9-Alpha winked out of existence so fast that the neighbouring universes felt a vacuum suck at their membranes. The hivemind\u2019s last, collective thought was a sensation of overwhelming heat, then nothing. The entire process took 0.0003 seconds.\n\nA third universe, 12-Vect, was a steampunk cosmos where clockwork gods turned the gears of reality. They prepared for a decade after hearing whispers of the Thronegate expansion. They forged a paradox engine designed to erase Godric\u2019s birth. The plan was elaborate, millennial in scope. But the chief clockmaker, a being named Kaelix, made a fatal error: he hypothesized that Godric\u2019s power must have a flaw\u2014perhaps it was tied to the stasis, and if they could recreate the conditions of the spell, they could lock him again. The thought germinated in Kaelix\u2019s mind for three seconds before he even began drafting the schematics.\n\nThe moment the speculation took form\u2014the merest flicker of \"weakness\"\u2014the universe responded. Deep in the throne room, Godric paused mid-conversation with Blake. A subtle warmth spread through his chest: the amplification rate that had been compounding for 10,000 years suddenly jumped, and that jump\u2019s rate itself jumped. Simultaneously, he became irrevocably immune to any temporal stasis, any spell mimicry, any attack predicated on the incomplete ritual. And he gained masterful, instant command over every nuance of Thorin\u2019s hereditary magic\u2014the very magic that had placed him in stasis\u2014able to deploy it or deny it to others as he pleased.\n\nKaelix, ignorant, spent years building the paradox engine. When it was finally activated, a beam of chronal energy lanced toward Godric\u2019s point of origin. But before it could reach the past, Godric plucked the beam from the timestream, held it between his thumb and forefinger like a splinter, and flicked it back. The engine exploded, freezing its operators in an eternal, agonizing moment. Kaelix found himself suspended, aware but immobile, as Godric\u2019s voice echoed in his skull: \"Your thought was your undoing. The very instant you considered a flaw, you fed me beyond your comprehension, and you sealed your fate. I have no weaknesses. You merely sharpened the blade that cuts you.\" The clockwork universe surrendered unconditionally that same day.\n\nSuch lessons propagated across the omniverse. More and more realms accepted surrender upon first contact. Those that didn\u2019t learned the taste of futility.\n\nTwenty years passed. Godric\u2019s rule became absolute, stretching across countless dimensions. But within the capital, a change occurred. Blake, with his merchant\u2019s pragmatism and quick laugh, spent hours with Godric in the library or walking the gardens. He never feared Godric after that first battle. He\u2019d snap at the omnipotent king when he found him brooding, and Godric would, to everyone\u2019s shock, apologize. Over time, the cruel, merciless edges softened. Godric began visiting orphanages, remembering his own daughters. He held public audiences where he listened, truly listened, to his subjects. His justice remained brutal toward enemies, but his warmth returned\u2014a fatherly hand on a child\u2019s head, a friendly jest with a tavern keeper.\n\nBlake, meanwhile, discovered old tomes in the palace archives that felt familiar in a way he couldn\u2019t explain. Spells that Thorin\u2019s ancestors had written seemed to call to him. Godric watched silently, offering guidance but never the secret of Blake\u2019s lineage. Blake assumed it was a side-effect of the Awakening. His son Josh, now twenty-two, often joined him, showing an even keener aptitude. And his daughter Rhea, though not a wizard, became a historian, cataloguing the forgotten millennia.\n\nOn a cool autumn evening, Godric sat on the throne\u2019s lower steps, sharing a flask of ale with Blake. \"You know,\" Godric said, staring at the star-laced sky, \"I once officiated a wedding. My daughter\u2019s. I was terrified I\u2019d stumble over the words.\" Blake laughed, the sound easy. \"You? Terrified?\" Godric nodded. \"I was a different man then. I think I\u2019m becoming him again, thanks to you.\" Blake clinked his cup against Godric\u2019s. \"You were always in there. Just needed someone to argue with.\"\n\nBlake\u2019s hair had greyed, his mutton chops white, but his back was straight. At fifty-eight, he was a figure of quiet power, the unofficial court wizard, though he still called himself a merchant. His son Josh apprenticed under him, and already the people whispered that the wizardly line of Olympus had returned\u2014though none dared speak it outright.\n\nIn the present day, Thronegate stands as the heart of the omniverse\u2019s most benevolent tyranny. The Awakened men handle disasters, mediate conflicts, and explore unknown dimensions, always suppressing their might to mortal levels unless the situation demands. Godric\u2019s law is simple: peace for those who accept it, annihilation for those who don\u2019t. And beneath the surface of that peace, the absolute terror of a god who can unmake everything with a stray thought keeps the rebellious tendencies of a million universes in check.\n\nThe final image: the capital square during the Festival of Dust, commemorating the day Olympus fell. Lanterns float on invisible currents. Godric, looking exactly as he did ten thousand years ago, stands on the royal balcony, his hand resting on Blake\u2019s shoulder. The crowd below roars with adoration, and Godric smiles\u2014a real smile, not the rictus of a tyrant. Blake says something that makes him laugh, and the sound carries across the plaza, warm and human. And yet, those who are perceptive notice that Godric\u2019s shadow doesn\u2019t quite align with the lantern light; it stretches, impossibly vast, into dimensions beyond seeing, a quiet reminder that their beloved king is, and always will be, the apex predator of all existence.\n\nNow, I need to ensure the word count is under 4000.
