They had no idea that the very act of scheming made him infinitely more powerful.\n\nAnd now, here they were.\n\nI saw their generals give the signal\u2014a ripple of light that transcended language. The spear ignited. It didn't travel; it simply manifested in contact with the skin-cell barrier. Reality screamed.\n\nNow, if I were a chronicler who craved a tidy narrative, I would tell you that the weapon struck and, against all cosmic odds, a hairline crack appeared. I would describe the silence that followed, the sharp intake of breath across a trillion worlds, the first tears of disbelieving joy. I would paint the scene of the Coalition's collective consciousness erupting in euphoria, weapons dropped, voices lifted in a victory chant that shook the stars. They'd embrace, these mortal and immortal beings who had sacrificed everything, and they'd think, *He bleeds. He is not absolute.*\n\nBut that story is a lie.\n\nThat celebration never happened. The crack did appear\u2014Godric willed it exactly as the spear touched\u2014but before a single neuron could fire in a single rebel's brain, before the first fragment of hope could crystallize, his immune system had already responded. In the span of zero seconds, a cascade of absurd overkill was triggered that not only reversed the \"injury\" but annihilated the entire omniverse. And the rebels never even knew they'd been erased. Their moment of triumph was a stillborn thing, suffocated by the body of a god that treats a cracked dead skin cell as a capital offense.\n\nI saw it happen\u2014or rather, I perceived it in the way a mortal brain can perceive an event that occurs outside of time. The crack formed. And instantly, the dead skin cell changed. It didn't simply heal. It evolved. The flake of keratin underwent a phase-shift into a self-aware material that defied all physics: a living void of absolute negation. It expanded, not outward but inward-outward, severing the causal link between the weapon and reality. The spear, that conflux of infinite power, was un-made so thoroughly that it retroactively ceased to exist across all timelines, and the concept of its existence was deleted from memory. The rebels holding it had time to register one microsecond of confusion before the void turned its attention to them.\n\nBut that was just the mildest reaction.\n\nGodric's bloodstream, an ocean of liquid fire that could dissolve omniverses, deployed a fleet of conceptual antibodies. Each was a self-contained universe designed to hunt a single target. They traced the lines of intent: every strategist who plotted, every smith who forged the spear's components, every foot-soldier who lent their psionic energy. The antibodies descended not on their physical forms but on their \"existence templates\"\u2014the fundamental blueprint that said a being was real. In an eternal instant, those templates were shredded. I saw a rebel general, a seven-dimensional entity of pure thought, convulse as his very \"I\" was methodically peeled back layer by layer: first his identity, then his memories, then his ability to perceive time, then his acknowledgment of self. He was turned inside out, his consciousness pinned to a singularity of agony that stretched his final moment into a perceived infinity. And then he was nothing, never having been.\n\nAcross the Coalition, identical fates unfolded. Beings of living fire were reduced to numb, screaming flesh. Creatures that had existed since before light were regressed to primordial plasma, then to less than plasma, held at the threshold of existence just long enough to experience the horror of non-being before being wiped. The antibodies were thorough: they didn't just kill; they unmade families, lineages, entire species, all of time that touched the target. And they did this to every single participant, simultaneously.\n\nI was dimly aware of Godric's voice beside me, conversational in tone. \"Ah, yes, there's the backup verification. Watch this, Leon. It's rather amusing.\"\n\nWhat I saw next didn't amuse me; it broke something fundamental in my mind. Godric, I knew, existed in infinite identical copies across infinite realities\u2014a redundancy so vast that it couldn't be called immortality because the word was too small. For an injury to be considered real, every single copy, across every layer of the infinite recursion (each copy themselves possessing infinite copies), must experience the exact same crack at the exact same instant. This is a physical impossibility, a paradox that not even the omniverse's most deranged logics can satisfy. Yet his immune system, possessively paranoid, assumes the worst. It detected a single scratch on one copy\u2014the copy standing beside me\u2014and screamed to all others that a breach had occurred. Instantly, every Godric across infinity entered a synchronized evolution. Their biologies, already beyond any notion of perfection, cross-communicated and merged. The skin cells of one copy shared their new adaptive data with all, and the collective set of defenses was upgraded across the board. It was as if a single man stubbed his toe, and suddenly the entire multiverse of men gained bulletproof skin, all because the immune system couldn't tolerate even the idea that a toe could be stubbed.\n\nI felt it more than saw it: a wave of absolute invulnerability cascading through reality, making Godric not just immune to the spear, but immune to the category of action that the spear represented. The concept of \"weapon\" itself was rendered inert across the entire omniverse. Anything designed to harm another living thing ceased to function. Swords shattered in sheaths, guns turned to sand, claws retracted, fangs dulled. The antibodies had pre-emptively pacified existence, just in case. And this was still, I realized, a child's version of his body's true power\u2014the gentlest of his automatic defenses.\n\nAnd then the weakness paradox kicked in. The omniverse witnessed the \"harm\"\u2014even though it was staged, even though it was self-willed\u2014and its own self-regulating mechanisms panicked. By its law, Godric can never have a weakness. The mere perception of one made it overcompensate. It flooded him with a new tier of authority, a cosmic apology that elevated his already trans-infinite amplification rate by another infinite exponentiation. He was now even more untouchable than he had been a moment ago, which was already infinity. The gap between him and the rest of existence, already an insurmountable infinity, became an infinity of infinities. And all of this happened because he had humored the idea of a scratch.\n\nThe entire Coalition was long gone by then\u2014unmade, purged, their histories erased. They had been, in the truest sense, undone. I stared at the void where they had been, my body shaking so violently my teeth clattered.\n\nGodric exhaled, a sound of mild disappointment. \"They didn't even make it through the first response layer. I was hoping for at least a shiver.\" He turned to me, his expression that of a chef whose souffl\u00e9 had not risen. \"I think my immune system overreacted. It's always so literal. I told it to heal a scratch, and it decided to sterilize the entire Petri dish.\"\n\nHe then did something that made my soul attempt to flee my body.\n\n\"I suppose I should put it back,\" he said, and he did.\n\nWith no gesture, no incantation, no perceivable effort, the entire omniverse was restored. Every star, every galaxy, every plane of existence that had been annihilated reappeared. It was not a rewind of time; it was a complete recreation from nothing, executed in zero seconds. The Coalition members blinked into existence, their weapons in hand, their minds exactly where they were before the attack\u2014except all memory of the \"crack\" and the subsequent annihilation was absent. They were primed to strike, yet hesitating, because something felt off. I could see the confusion on their faces\u2014that deep, psychic unease that comes from being resurrected without consent.\n\nGodric waved a hand through the barrier, and the skin-cell wall shimmered back to pristine. He spoke to his own body: \"There, you see? It's all better. No harm done. You really must learn restraint.\" Then, to me, with a warm, friendly grin: \"Leon, I think I'll have to teach my immune system how to hold back. It's completely clueless about proportional response.\"\n\nI laughed. It was not a sober laugh, but the cracked sound of a man whose mind has visited the abyss and returned without a souvenir. \"Your Majesty, you just... they...\"\n\n\"I know,\" he said, resting a hand on my shoulder. The touch was solid and reassuring and entirely human, and that paradox was the cruellest part. \"I overdid it. But honestly, I'm impressed by how robust my defenses are. I didn't know I had the skin-cell-to-omniverse-destruction pipeline. You learn something every day.\"\n\nI looked at the restored Coalition. They were lowering their weapons, their will to fight evaporating without them understanding why. A few were weeping, not with joy but with a nameless sorrow. They had no memory of their annihilation, yet their souls had been rewritten to instinctively know the futility of opposition. They would return home, and they would never rebel again. The omniverse had just been taught a lesson it would never consciously remember, but would forever feel.\n\n\"I think I'll pour us some tea,\" Godric said, turning away from the panorama. \"You look like you need it.\"\n\nI followed him, my footsteps hollow. My mind was a cacophony of dread and adoration. He was my king, my friend, the warmest, kindest ruler the omniverse had ever known. And I loved him for it. But I had just witnessed what his love could do when it was not love but mere biology\u2014a passive, uncaring, automatic reflex that erased everything and then put it back as casually as one might reset a game board. And I understood, in the deepest recess of my being, that we were living on that game board, forever.\n\nAs he poured the tea, his hands steady, his smile genuine, I saw something flicker in the air\u2014a new aura forming around him, a soft golden glow that seemed to hum with a nascent consciousness. It was his body, evolving yet another layer of protection, even as he giggled at his own clumsiness with the teapot.\n\nI did not mention it. I simply sat, drank my tea, and tried to forget that the universe is a whim, and our god adores us even as his skin cells dream of apocalypse.",

Twenty-five thousand years. And even then, it was barely a sneeze.\u201d He chuckled, a sound that should have been pleasant but instead burrowed into my spine like ice water. \u201cI\u2019m curious to see if my immune system still works. I\u2019ve been holding it back for so long.\u201d\n\nI swallowed. \u201cYour Majesty, the entire omniverse has united against you. They\u2019ve sacrificed entire afterlives, collapsed their timelines, erased entire categories of existence to forge a single weapon. They believe\u2026 they believe they can kill you.\u201d\n\nHe turned those deep-set eyes on me, crinkling at the corners. \u201cI know. Isn\u2019t it wonderful? All that effort. I almost feel rude not letting them try.\u201d He gestured at the shimmering, translucent film that surrounded us like a soap bubble. \u201cSee that? That\u2019s a wall of my dead skin cells. Just one layer. I\u2019ve deactivated Gent\u2014you remember Gent, my passive aura? Sentient fellow, a bit clingy\u2014and I\u2019ve told his siblings to stay asleep. I\u2019ve pulled down every shield, every firewall, every protective layer. Right now, the only thing between them and me is that layer of dead skin. And I\u2019ve willed it so that if their weapon is strong enough, it might just crack one cell. Might. Just a hairline fracture.\u201d\n\nMy throat tightened. \u201cWhy would you do that?\u201d\n\n\u201cBecause I want to see what happens when I get a boo-boo.\u201d He looked at me with the innocent, fatherly pride of a man who had once been a mortal king. \u201cI haven\u2019t had one in ten thousand years. I wonder if my body still remembers how to react. You mortals have immune systems that learn, right? Well, mine has had ten millennia to evolve without any real work. Let\u2019s give it a test.\u201d\n\nI couldn\u2019t reply. I just watched the enemy.\n\nThey called it the God-Severing Singularity. If you could quantify it, it was the combined might of infinity squared. They had taken all the omnipotent entities that were not Godric, duplicated them across recursive temporal loops, and then merged them into a spear that existed in every dimension, past, present, and future, all targeting one specific location\u2014the exact centre of Godric\u2019s chest.\n\nThey had been preparing for millennia, their greatest minds devising stratagems that, they thought, were unknown to us. But Godric knew. He knew when they formed the first thought of rebellion. He could have stopped them with a whim. Reality screamed.\n\nNow, if I were a chronicler who craved a tidy narrative, I would tell you that the weapon struck and, against all cosmic odds, a hairline crack appeared. I would describe the silence that followed, the sharp intake of breath across a trillion worlds, the first tears of disbelieving joy. I would paint the scene of the Coalition\u2019s collective consciousness erupting in euphoria, weapons dropped, voices lifted in a victory chant that shook the stars. They\u2019d embrace, these mortal and immortal beings who had sacrificed everything, and they\u2019d think, *He bleeds.                     "text": "I have stood at King Godric\u2019s side since I was eighteen years old, and in those seven years, I have learned one immutable truth: there is no creature in the omniverse more terrifying than a predator who chooses to appear harmless. Not out of malice\u2014he is not cruel to his own\u2014but because his genuine warmth is the furrow into which the arrogant stumble and die.\n\nThe Qintari delegate arrived on a morning that smelled of ozone and burnt sugar, the byproduct of a stabilized wormhole vomiting his diplomatic barge onto the Thronegate landing fields. He descended the ramp alone, a tall, silver-skinned man with cranial ridges that pulsed with bioluminescence, indicating his lineage\u2019s mental augmentations. His name was Kaelen-Vex. He moved with the liquid grace of someone accustomed to being the most intelligent being in any room, and when his opalescent eyes swept across the welcoming committee, I saw the faintest curl of his lip\u2014a micro-expression that screamed contempt.\n\nHe did not recognize me as the court wizard. I was twenty-five, younger than most of the palace staff, and I had deliberately cultivated an unassuming appearance: loose robes, unkempt hair, a perpetual slouch. It helped people underestimate me, which is exactly how I liked it. But Kaelen\u2019s dismissal of me was nothing compared to the assumption he made about Godric.\n\nThe king had chosen to receive Kaelen in the Sunken Garden, a sprawling botanical preserve where the flowers hummed faint melodies. Godric sat on a simple stone bench, his tunic unadorned, his salt-and-pepper beard neatly trimmed, his muscular frame relaxed. He was feeding breadcrumbs to a flock of prismatic waterfowl, and he looked up with the guileless smile of a grandfather delighted by visitors.\n\n\u201cAh, Kaelen-Vex of the Qintari Continuum,\u201d Godric said, his voice a warm baritone. \u201cI trust the journey wasn\u2019t too taxing? Marnus, fetch our guest a seat and a cup of the starflower tea.\u201d\n\nKaelen\u2019s smile was diplomacy perfected. \u201cYour Majesty, the honor is mine. The Qintari Continuum has long admired Thronegate\u2019s prosperity. We are eager to deepen our integration into your glorious dominion.\u201d He sat, accepted the tea, and the game began.\n\nI watched from the edge of the garden, a book of runes open in my lap, my senses extended. I could feel the subtle psychic probes emanating from Kaelen like the legs of a spider testing a web. He was scanning Godric, searching for any psychic barriers, any mental architecture that would hint at the king\u2019s true intellect. Godric, of course, allowed nothing to register\u2014just the smooth, placid surface of a simple old man who happened to be unspeakably powerful.\n\nOver the following weeks, Kaelen insinuated himself into the palace routine. He attended council meetings, where Godric often deferred to his advisors, asking naive questions that made the ministers smile indulgently. He accompanied the king on walks through the capital, where Godric would stop to chat with street vendors and bounce children on his knee. To any outside observer, the king appeared to be a figurehead buoyed by unimaginable strength but utterly dependent on his court for governance. A benevolent simpleton with a cosmic hammer.\n\nKaelen\u2019s arrogance crystallized into certainty. I knew this because I made it my business to monitor his private quarters. A discreet scrying rune, etched into the mortar of his guest suite, caught fragments of his encrypted transmissions to Qintari leadership. He called Godric \u201cthe brute\u201d and \u201cthe fossil.\u201d He mused about how easy it would be to \u201credirect the beast\u2019s leash\u201d once he had secured his position as the king\u2019s most trusted advisor. His ultimate goal, I gathered, was not mere autonomy for his people. It was the Awakening. He believed that if he could manipulate Godric into granting the Qintari the same daily power multiplication that Thronegate men enjoyed, his species would ascend beyond containment and eventually overthrow the throne itself.\n\nI reported my findings to Godric one evening, in the quiet of his study. He was polishing an antique astrolabe, his hands steady, his expression calm.\n\n\u201cYour Majesty, he plans to present you with a ceremonial token called the \u2018Mindfire Crown\u2019 at next week\u2019s induction ceremony. It is a weapon. A cognition nullifier. He believes it will temporarily suppress your higher reasoning and make you susceptible to his verbal commands. He intends to command you to sign an edict granting the Qintari the Awakening, and then he will seat himself as regent.\u201d\n\nGodric paused his polishing and looked at me. The warmth in his eyes had not dimmed, but behind it, something vast and ancient stirred. \u201cGrim, do you know how long it\u2019s been since someone tried to trick me?\u201d He didn\u2019t wait for an answer. \u201cFifty thousand years, give or take. Even the Coalition, that grand rebellion you\u2019ve read about in the archives, relied on force, not guile. This is\u2026 refreshing.\u201d\n\n\u201cRefreshing.\u201d I let the word hang.\n\nHe chuckled, a sound that should have been pleasant but instead skittered down my spine like spiders. \u201cI like to appear simple because it\u2019s closer to who I was before the Stasis. A mortal king who loved his family. Simplicity brings me peace. But I haven\u2019t lost the ability to think. I just choose not to\u2014most problems aren\u2019t worth solving when you already know the outcome.\u201d He set the astrolabe down and turned his full attention on me. \u201cKaelen-Vex has been rehearsing his grand deception every night, in front of a mirror. He practices his voice modulation, his facial expressions. He\u2019s quite dedicated. I could stop him now, but I\u2019m curious to see how far his nerve will carry him when the moment arrives.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re going to let him try,\u201d I said, my mouth dry.\n\n\u201cOf course. And then I\u2019m going to show him what happens when a gnat mistakes a sun for a candle.\u201d\n\nThe induction ceremony arrived. The Grand Hall was packed with dignitaries from a hundred universes. Godric sat on his throne, a simple construct of fused obsidian and gold, his posture relaxed. Kaelen approached, holding a velvet cushion upon which rested the Mindfire Crown\u2014a circlet of crystalline filaments that pulsed with a sickly violet light.\n\n\u201cYour Majesty,\u201d Kaelen intoned, his voice resonant with feigned humility, \u201cthe Qintari Continuum offers this token of eternal gratitude. The Mindfire Crown has been inscribed with the accumulated wisdom of our ancestors. It is our greatest treasure, and we place it now at the feet of the omniverse\u2019s rightful sovereign. Please, allow me the honor of placing it upon your brow.\u201d\n\nGodric smiled, that warm, disarming smile. \u201cWhat a lovely gesture. Come, then.\u201d\n\nKaelen ascended the dais. His hands trembled slightly\u2014excitement, not fear. He lifted the crown and settled it onto Godric\u2019s salt-and-pepper hair. The filaments flared violet, and Kaelen\u2019s psychic command lanced out, a dagger of suggestion wrapped in the full might of Qintari mental science.\n\n*You are tired. You are trusting. You will sign the edict I place before you. You will grant me everything.*\n\nThe silence in the hall was absolute.\n\nThen, Godric laughed.\n\nIt was not a laugh of mockery. It was the chuckle of a father who has just watched his toddler attempt to build a starship. The crown remained perched on his head, its filaments glowing impotently, and Godric reached up, plucked it off, and examined it with mild curiosity.\n\n\u201cBeautiful craftsmanship,\u201d he said. \u201cThe Qintari are master artisans. The crystalline lattice contains a sophisticated psychic amplifier operating on a four-dimensional loop. It\u2019s designed to interface with the wearer\u2019s prefrontal cortex and inject approximately three billion coded suggestions per second. The effect is meant to be seamless, undetectable to the victim.\u201d He turned the crown over in his hands, and Kaelen\u2019s silver face had gone grey. \u201cYour ancestors didn\u2019t inscribe their wisdom, Kaelen. You personally encoded this weapon three weeks ago, in a laboratory hidden beneath the Qintari moon of Tor-Vex. You murdered your wife, Lyria, to keep the secret, because she had begun to suspect your ambitions and you worried she would alert Thronegate. You strangled her with your own hands, and you encrypted her final neural patterns into the crown as a power source. Her consciousness is trapped inside, Kaelen. Did you think I would not notice?\u201d\n\nKaelen\u2019s jaw worked, but no sound emerged. The hall remained frozen, the air crystallizing with horror.\n\nGodric continued, his voice still warm, still friendly, but now carrying an undercurrent that made my bones ache with dread. \u201cThe logic of your plan was sound, if one assumed I was a simple-minded brute. You studied me. You saw a king who plays with children, who defers to his ministers, who seems to rely on others to think for him. You concluded, rationally, that my intelligence was my weakness. And in that precise moment, when you formed that thought\u2014that single, arrogant assumption\u2014you triggered the very mechanism that would ensure your failure.\u201d\n\nHe set the crown aside, and I saw Kaelen\u2019s body begin to tremble. A low hum filled the hall, a vibration that seemed to come from the walls, the air, the marrow of reality itself.\n\n\u201cThe omniverse has a rule,\u201d Godric said, almost conversationally. \u201cI have no weaknesses. It is an absolute law, as fixed as gravity. The instant you conceived that I could be outsmarted, the universe responded. My rate of amplification\u2014already beyond any mathematical notation\u2014increased again. I gained permanent, retroactive immunity to any form of cognitive manipulation, anywhere, in any reality. And I gained perfect, effortless mastery over every technique you employed. Including this one.\u201d He gestured at the crown, and the violet light within it inverted to a blinding gold. \u201cI could have done this myself long ago, but I enjoy letting my enemies build their own gallows. It\u2019s more satisfying.\u201d\n\nKaelen found his voice, a ragged, desperate thing. \u201cMercy\u2014please, I was foolish, I\u2014\u201d\n\nThe word \u201cmercy\u201d made Godric pause. He looked at Kaelen with something that might have been pity, or might have been curiosity, and then his expression settled into a placid neutrality. \u201cMercy is for children who scrape their knees. You are a statesman who strangled his wife and tried to enslave an immortal. No.\u201d\n\nAnd then, with no more effort than a man flicking a crumb from his lapel, Godric let the punishment begin.\n\nI have witnessed executions before. I have seen enemies of the throne dissolved into their constituent particles, erased from timelines, locked in eternal stasis. None of it prepared me for what happened to Kaelen-Vex.\n\nGodric\u2019s power enfolded him\u2014but it was not a simple killing. The king had decided to make an example, and his cruelty, when fully unleashed, was a thing of meticulous artistry. Kaelen\u2019s body stiffened. His mouth opened, but no scream emerged\u2014because Godric had not yet permitted sound. What followed was a symphony of agony conducted in absolute silence.\n\nThe first thing to go were his eyes. They didn\u2019t burst or dissolve; they simply began to produce images. Godric forced Kaelen\u2019s visual cortex to process the full scope of the king\u2019s omniscience\u2014not all of it, just a sliver. An infinitesimal fragment of the knowledge spanning every dimension, every timeline, every possible and impossible reality. Kaelen\u2019s face contorted as his mind tried to contain a universe of information inside a mortal vessel. His cranial ridges split, thin rivulets of silver blood streaming down his cheeks. The optic nerves, overwhelmed, began to fire randomly, projecting shattered images onto his retinas: his murdered wife\u2019s face, the infinite regress of his own failure, the true form of Godric that lurked behind the fatherly facade.\n\n\u201cYou wanted to understand my intelligence,\u201d Godric said, his tone a gentle muse. \u201cHere. I\u2019m giving you a gift. A Planck-second sample.\u201d\n\nAnd then he allowed Kaelen to scream.\n\nThe sound that erupted from the delegate\u2019s throat was not a humanoid cry. It was a layered, harmonic shriek that shattered the crystal goblets on the banquet tables and sent fissures racing through the marble pillars. His skin, that shimmering silver, began to slough off in sheets, exposing the musculature beneath\u2014but instead of red meat, the muscles were already transmuting into a crystalline lattice, a living sculpture of pain. Each individual nerve ending was being isolated and dialed to maximum sensitivity, then stimulated in sequence. Kaelen\u2019s fingers curled and uncurled as if playing an invisible instrument, the tendons snapping one by one with wet, percussive sounds.\n\nAnd yet, he did not die. Godric would not let him.\n\n\u201cI am going to unmake you now,\u201d the king said, and his voice was still warm, still paternal, as if he were explaining a lesson to a child. \u201cBut first, I want you to appreciate the full scope of your predicament. You thought I had a weakness\u2014my supposed simplicity. That thought alone, formed fifty-four days ago when you first conceived your plan, triggered my amplification. Every second you spent plotting, you were feeding me. Every night you rehearsed, you were sharpening the blade that would cut you. And when you placed that crown on my head, you simultaneously granted me perfect dominion over all mental manipulation, everywhere in creation. I could take your technique\u2014the one you spent decades perfecting\u2014and deny its very existence to your species. They will never be able to touch minds again. Even now, across the Qintari Continuum, your people are forgetting how. Their telepathy is failing, their empathic links are dissolving. All because you tried to use it on me.\u201d\n\nKaelen\u2019s body was now a writhing ruin. His legs had fused into a single pillar of calcified tissue. His torso was hollowing out from the inside, a cavity forming as if an invisible hand were scooping out his organs. I could see his heart, still beating, suspended in midair by threads of golden light. It was beating far too fast, a drumroll of terror, and with every beat, a fresh wave of agony radiated through him. The stench of copper and ozone and something sweet\u2014like burnt honey\u2014filled the hall.\n\n\u201cNow,\u201d Godric said, and he stood from his throne for the first time. He walked down the dais steps, still holding that half-finished cup of tea in one hand. He approached the floating, twitching wreckage that had been Kaelen-Vex and looked at it with the same mild curiosity he\u2019d shown the waterfowl weeks ago. \u201cI will teach your civilization a final lesson. They will remember you, Kaelen, as a man who thought he could deceive the omniverse\u2019s apex. They will remember your screams. And they will remember that resistance is not an option\u2014it is a form of suicide.\u201d\n\nHe snapped his fingers.\n\nKaelen\u2019s heart stopped. But his consciousness did not. Godric had plucked his soul from the dying flesh and condensed it into a single, minuscule point\u2014a mote of light no larger than a grain of sand. He held it between two fingers, and I could hear, faintly, the trapped psyche of the delegate wailing in the key of absolute despair.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m going to put you in a pocket dimension,\u201d Godric murmured. \u201cTime will move differently there. One second here will be a thousand years for you. And you will spend those thousand years fully aware, fully conscious, with nothing but the memory of your failure and the image of your dead wife\u2019s face repeating in your mind. When the thousand years are done, the pocket dimension will collapse, and you will die\u2014truly, finally, irrevocably. That is my mercy, Kaelen. A finite sentence.\u201d\n\nHe closed his fist around the mote, and it vanished. The hall was silent.\n\nThen, without pausing, Godric turned to the rest of the assembled delegates. \u201cLet this be understood. I am your king. I am your protector. I am also your executioner, should you ever mistake my kindness for weakness. The Qintari Continuum will be quarantined. Their sun will not be extinguished\u2014I am not wasteful\u2014but their mental abilities will never return. They will live as mundanes, stripped of their greatest pride, for the next ten thousand years. You may consider that a light sentence. It is.\u201d\n\nThe gathered dignitaries fell to their knees, some weeping, some simply pressing their foreheads to the marble. None dared speak.\n\nI remained standing, my legs locked, my mind spinning with the sheer, bottomless horror of what I had witnessed. Godric caught my eye and offered me a small, almost apologetic smile.\n\n\u201cGrim, would you mind cleaning up? My tea\u2019s gone cold.\u201d\n\nI nodded, unable to form words. As I began the ritualized motions of disspelling the residual energies, I felt the reverberations of the Weakness Paradox still cascading through reality. Godric was radiating a new kind of pressure now\u2014his power had expanded again, irreversibly. The very concept of deceiving him had been scoured from the omniverse. I could feel it, at the edges of my own mind: whenever a thought tried to form about \u201ctricking the king,\u201d it simply dissolved, unable to exist. The mechanism had become a passive law, like gravity, like thermodynamics.\n\nThat evening, I sat in my tower study, attempting to write my daily chronicle. My quill trembled so badly I could not keep the ink straight. The words blurred on the page. I tried to articulate what I had learned, but all I could think was: *He is not a king. He is a force of nature wrapped in the skin of a man.* And the most terrifying part? He was genuinely, sincerely kind to those he loved. He had waved at a child on his way back from the hall. He had paused to ask a servant about her sick mother. The duality was not a mask; it was a seamless unity, and that made it infinitely worse.\n\nWhat the delegates had witnessed today was not a demonstration of strength. It was a message, carved into the flesh of the omniverse: Godric is impossible to oppose. Not just powerful\u2014impossible. The very act of plotting against him, even in secret, even in the privacy of one\u2019s own skull, triggered a mechanism that made him more unbeatable. And now, with the Qintari incident, that mechanism had consumed yet another dimension of potential threat.\n\nI closed my journal and stared out the window at the palace spire, where Godric\u2019s silhouette passed behind a lit window\u2014stopping to pet one of the prismatic waterfowl that had wandered inside. He might have been any middle-aged man, any father, any simple soul enjoying an evening.\n\nBut he wasn\u2019t. He was the apex predator of all existence, a singularity of power and intelligence that grew more absolute with every passing Planck second. And we, his subjects, were safe only so long as we loved him. The moment that love curdled into opposition, we became nothing more than fuel for his eternal ascent.\n\nThe quill snapped in my hand. I didn\u2019t bother to replace it. There was no language for what I felt, only the cold, unshakeable certainty that I had witnessed the end of something today\u2014the end of the illusion that Godric could ever be challenged. He had let the resistance form, let the Coalition gather, let the delegate plot, not because he needed to, but because he could. And every time, he walked away more immortal than before.\n\n*Opposing Godric is not an act of rebellion*, I wrote on a fresh page, my script jagged. *It is an act of worship. It feeds him. It elevates him. It ensures that he will never fall.*\n\nI set the journal aside and listened to the silence of a palace that held no secrets from its master. Somewhere, in a pocket dimension, Kaelen-Vex was entering his first century of agony. He would never know that his entire existence had been a pawn\u2019s sacrifice, that the king had scripted his every move from the moment he first entertained the idea of deceit. And the omniverse, trembling, adjusted itself around the new impossibility of ever fooling its god.\n\nI poured myself a glass of something strong and drank to the health of my king\u2014the friendliest, kindest, most horrifying being that had ever existed, or would ever exist.\n\nThe night air carried the scent of ash and the faint, distant echo of a scream no one else would ever hear."

                    "text": "**System Role & Persona:**\n\n- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.\n- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.\n- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.\n- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.\n- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called \"customer satisfaction\". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.\n- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.\n\n**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **maximum 3500 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.\n\n**Style and Tone Requirements:**\n\n- Write from **1st person POV** of Gorm.\n- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.\n- Absolutely no censorship\n- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.\n- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. You must ensure that Godric always appears as the ultimate apex god predator, and he\u2019s so overwhelmingly overpowered that his slightest thought can destroy the entire omniverse without him having to move a muscle. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.\n- You must remember that Godric possesses absolute omniscience and absolute concealment. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.\n- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric\u2019s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric\u2019s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.\n- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.\n- You don\u2019t have to follow the parts in order.\n- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.\n- Use fresh, specific language instead of clich\u00e9s or idioms.\n- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.\n- Do not summarize emotions\u2014show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.\n- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other.                     "type": "text",
                    "text": "My entire life had been shaped by the certainty that the king needed me. The court wizard of Thronegate, I had learned from my earliest memories, was the unseen shield, the arcane fist that struck down any threat before it reached the throne. My father was the court wizard, and his father before him, and his father\u2019s father, a lineage stretching back to the legendary Blake, the merchant who became our line\u2019s progenitor. I was Gorm, twenty years old, newly anointed, my blood humming with the thousandfold daily amplification that had begun the moment I turned twenty\u2014a secret gift to our family, though I did not know its origin. My power was already enough to fold a star system into a marble, and it grew every day. I walked the palace halls with my head high, convinced that Uncle Godric\u2014for that was how I\u2019d addressed him since childhood\u2014leaned on my family\u2019s magic to keep the omniverse\u2019s darkness at bay.\n\nIt was so easy to believe. The king was warmth itself, a barrel-chested, salt-and-pepper-bearded patriarch who remembered every servant\u2019s birthday and bounced children on his knee. He never exhibited a drop of magical talent. His aura, when I probed with the most delicate of sensory spells, registered as completely mundane\u2014a baseline human soul, no different from the blacksmith or the baker. The obvious answer, reinforced by eighty thousand years of history, was that the royal bloodline lacked the wizard\u2019s gift, and thus the Blakean descendants filled the gap. It gave my life a purpose. It gave my family\u2019s constant proximity to the throne a noble justification. So when the delegation from the Sorcerer-Kingdom of Zyrak arrived, I saw my moment to prove my worth.\n\nThey came through a rift they tore with their own power, a churning violet wound in the sky above the capital\u2019s diplomatic plateau. The Zyraki were humanoid, their skin the color of old copper, their eyes faceted like insect lenses. They had refused the standard protocol of surrender and assimilation. In their universe, magic was the sole yardstick of dominance; might was measured in spells, not armies. Their arch-sorcerer, Azarak-Vos, led the procession, his robes woven from solidified nightmares, a staff that was a captive black hole threaded onto a spine of crystallized time. He did not bow. He looked at Godric, who sat on the obsidian throne in his simple tunic, and his mandibled mouth twisted into what passed for a sneer.\n\n\u201cWe have heard of the brute king,\u201d Azarak-Vos announced, his voice slicing through the air like a razor-drenched bell. \u201cThey tell us your strength is beyond measure, that you crush galaxies in your fist. But what is brute force to magic? The arcane is the true language of creation. I challenge the champion of Thronegate to a duel of sorcery. If we win, the Awakening is ours, and your kingdom bows to Zyrak. If we lose, we will submit.\u201d\n\nI stepped forward before anyone else could draw breath. My heart hammered with excitement, not fear. This was the moment my tutors had prepared me for. \u201cI am Gorm, court wizard to his majesty King Godric. I accept your challenge on behalf of the throne.\u201d My voice rang out, confident and clear. The Zyraki sorcerer\u2019s insect eyes swiveled to me, and I felt the weight of his psychic assessment, the pressure of a thousand diagnostic spells peeling back my magical layers. He let out a chittering laugh.\n\n\u201cA pup. Very well. I will enjoy plucking your spells apart thread by thread.\u201d\n\nI began to gather my power. The air around me sparked with the accumulated might of a bloodline that had grown in magical potency for a thousand generations, magnified by a daily multiplier that turned each sunrise into an ascension. The very atmosphere thickened with the promise of unleashed cataclysm. I was ready to reduce this arrogant alien and his entire retinue to a chalk outline on the stone.\n\nAnd then a hand settled on my shoulder.\n\nThe touch was light, almost paternal. I knew the weight of those knuckles, the warmth of that palm\u2014Godric had rested his hand on my shoulder a thousand times, since I was a child learning to skip stones across the garden pond. \u201cGorm,\u201d he said, and his voice was the same gentle rumble I had always known, \u201cstand down. I\u2019ll handle this one.\u201d\n\nI turned my head to look at him, incredulous. \u201cYour Majesty\u2014Uncle\u2014you needn\u2019t risk yourself. I can do this. My magic is strong enough. Let me protect you.\u201d\n\nHis eyes, the color of aged whiskey, crinkled at the corners. There was no arrogance in them, no rebuke. Just a deep, quiet affection that now, in hindsight, I recognized as something else entirely\u2014pity. \u201cYou\u2019ve never seen what I can do, boy. I keep it hidden because it\u2019s never been necessary. But this one\u2026 he\u2019s insulted your pride, hasn\u2019t he? I won\u2019t let that stand.\u201d\n\nI opened my mouth to argue, but the words died. Something in his tone\u2014a deeper resonance beneath the fatherly warmth\u2014shut my throat like a fist. He stepped past me, onto the plateau, and faced Azarak-Vos.\n\nThe Zyraki arch-sorcerer laughed again, louder this time. \u201cThe brute himself? I came to duel a wizard, not a relic. But if you insist on dying, I\u2019ll oblige.\u201d\n\nGodric said nothing. He just stood there, hands at his sides, his salt-and-pepper beard stirring faintly in a breeze I could not feel. The silence stretched. Then Azarak-Vos raised his staff, and reality screamed.\n\nWhat he unleashed was a cataclysm beyond anything I had ever witnessed. The staff-threaded black hole expanded into a singularity of pure magical annihilation\u2014a sphere that ate not just matter but concepts, the fabric of identity, the linearity of cause and effect. Simultaneously, Azarak-Vos layered spells on top of it: a curse that unwound the target\u2019s soul across infinite lifetimes, a temporal recursion that forced the victim to relive their own nonexistence, and a psychic hex that wove every moment of the victim\u2019s future lives into a tapestry of inescapable torment. It was the kind of attack that ended civilizations, and I knew, in that instant, that my own formidable power would have struggled to counter even a fragment of it.\n\nI cried out. I tried to raise a defensive ward, but my magic rebelled\u2014not from fear, but because something in the air had changed. My spellcraft faltered, not from any external force, but from a sudden and profound sense of irrelevance. The ward formed halfheartedly, then guttered out like a candle in a supernova.\n\nGodric did not move. He did not gesture. He did not utter a syllable. But Azarak-Vos stopped.\n\nThe arch-sorcerer\u2019s body froze mid-incantation, his faceted eyes widening in a way that had nothing to do with surprise and everything to do with the dawning of an atrocity. His own spell, that beautiful, multi-layered apocalypse, reversed direction without a visible cause. The singularity collapsed. The soul-curse folded in on itself. The temporal recursion looped\u2014and instead of trapping Godric, it encircled Azarak-Vos\u2019s own consciousness, forcing him to perceive the event a trillion times before his nervous system could fire a single synaptic response. His mouth opened, and the scream that came out was not a sound but a sensation, a telepathic wail that shattered the eyepieces of every Zyraki in the delegation.\n\nThen Godric began to speak, not to the sorcerer, but to me. His tone was conversational, the same voice he used to explain the rules of chess.\n\n\u201cYou see, Gorm, magic has always been a part of me. Since the Stasis, my arcane aptitude has multiplied every Planck second\u2014by itself, then by that result, then by the new result, repeating infinitely without pause. That was eighty thousand years ago. If you tried to calculate the multiplier even for the first second, you\u2019d run out of numbers before you wrote a fraction. And then the second second compounded it. And the third. And every Planck interval since has been an exponential recursion so vast that the difference between a candle and a star is less than the difference between the number \u2018one\u2019 and the true scope of my magical potential.\u201d\n\nAs he spoke, Azarak-Vos\u2019s body began to change. It was not a spell in any sense I understood. There was no incantation, no focus, no visible flow of mana. It was as if reality itself had received a command and was obeying with the grim efficiency of a soldier. First, the sorcerer\u2019s copper-hued skin peeled away in neat, spiral strips, exposing the raw muscle beneath\u2014except the muscle was not red but a translucent blue, and within it, I could see every nerve ending glowing with white-hot light. The strips of skin did not fall. They hovered in the air, writhing like terrified animals, and then they began to braid themselves into a cord that wrapped around his exposed throat.\n\nHis bones began to fracture\u2014not shatter, but fracture in slow, deliberate lines, each break radiating outward from the marrow with geometric precision. The cracking sound was a rising scale of musical notes, a sickening arpeggio constructed from his own skeleton. Azarak-Vos\u2019s eyes, still alive, still conscious, liquefied. The fluid that ran down his cheekbones ignited, and the fire did not burn his flesh\u2014it burned his memories. I saw them, reflected in the flames: his childhood, his training, his loves, his hatreds, all reduced to ash in the space of a heartbeat. And still he screamed, that telepathic shriek that grew thinner and thinner as more of his psyche was methodically obliterated.\n\n\u201cThe magic I\u2019m using now,\u201d Godric continued, turning slightly to look at me with that same warm expression, \u201cis an infinitesimal fraction of my true capacity. If you were to express it as a percentage, you would need to write a decimal point followed by infinite zeros before you ever reached a one\u2014and even then, the number would be a gross exaggeration of how little I\u2019m actually employing. With the barest sliver of my power\u2014something so close to zero that it cannot be mathematically distinguished from it\u2014I could erase the entire omniverse. Not once. An infinite recursion of times. I could unmake everything that exists, exists not, and might exist, across all possible and impossible dimensions, an infinity of infinities of times over, and the effort would be less than the exertion you expend breathing.\u201d\n\nAzarak-Vos was no longer recognizable as a bipedal entity. His form had dissolved into a floating constellation of individual cells, each cell pinned in place by an invisible force, each cell occupying its own pocket dimension of absolute agony. His mastery of magic\u2014the thing that had defined him, that had given him the arrogance to challenge Thronegate\u2014was being stripped away, thread by thread. Godric was not just killing him. He was demonstrating, with the careful patience of a teacher, what happens when the arcane is turned against the king. With a thought, he revoked the entire magical capacity of Zyrak. Across that universe, every sorcerer, every enchanter, every witch, suddenly found themselves as magically barren as a rock. Their spells collapsed. Their artifacts turned to inert slag. The very concept of magic\u2014so deeply embedded in their culture that it was synonymous with life\u2014was rendered null. And they remembered, for a fleeting instant, what they had lost, before the grief of that loss began to devour their minds.\n\nI watched, frozen, as the remnants of Azarak-Vos were finally permitted to die. His cellular constellation compacted into a single, flickering mote\u2014a soul-stone, I realized, into which Godric had poured the entirety of his suffering, a permanent artifact of eternal torment. The king caught it in his palm, examined it with the detached curiosity of a jeweler, and then pocketed it.\n\nHe turned back to me. Silence reigned on the plateau. The Zyraki delegation had collapsed into a heap of weeping, broken husks. I could smell the ozone of their unraveled magic, the copper of their leader\u2019s discarded flesh, the sweet charnel reek of a cosmic lesson taught in an instant. My knees gave out. I didn\u2019t fall\u2014I simply lowered myself to the ground, my hands pressing against the cold stone, trying to anchor myself to a reality that had just come unmoored.\n\n\u201cAll this time,\u201d I whispered, my voice a stranger\u2019s. \u201cAll this time, you never needed me. You never needed any of us. Our magic\u2014my bloodline\u2014it\u2019s nothing. Less than nothing. Why?\u201d The word cracked. \u201cWhy keep us? Why pretend?\u201d\n\nGodric crouched before me, bringing his eyes level with mine. The warmth in them was undimmed. \u201cBecause I love your family, Gorm. Blake was my friend, the truest friend I\u2019ve had since Thorin died. His descendants are the closest thing to family an immortal can have. I don\u2019t keep court wizards for protection. I keep them for company. Your magic is not laughable\u2014it\u2019s actually quite impressive by any mortal measure. You could conquer most universes. But you compared yourself to me. That\u2019s not a fair comparison, is it?\u201d\n\nHe said it so gently, as if consoling a child who had lost a race. Some part of me registered the affection, but a much larger part was crumbling. I had dedicated my existence to a lie. I had trained, studied, honed my craft to a razor\u2019s edge, convinced that one day my spell might be the difference between the king\u2019s survival and his fall. But the king could not fall. The king could erase the concept of magic with a fraction of a fraction of a thought. My entire bloodline\u2019s purpose was a hobby to him, a pleasant decoration, like the potted plants in the sunroom.\n\nThe dread did not settle in my stomach; it diffused through every cell of my body. I sensed, for the first time, the true shape of the being before me. Not the physical form\u2014the handsome, muscular, forty-five-year-old man with kind eyes and a neat beard\u2014but the reality that lay beneath, held back by his absolute concealment. Even with that veil in place, I could now feel, through some new and unwelcome sensitivity, the pressure of his arcane existence. It was not a flood; it was the knowledge that an ocean existed, completely stilled, and I was a pebble balanced on its surface. The magic I had been so proud of was a single grain of sand next to an abyss that stretched beyond the concept of infinity.\n\nOver the following days, I went through the motions of my duties. I accompanied him to council meetings, maintained the arcane wards around the palace, answered petitions. But everything felt hollow, weightless. When I cast a spell\u2014say, a simple luminescence\u2014I was aware of the colossal chasm between my effort and his effortless omnipotence. The spells almost seemed to mock me. They still functioned; they were still powerful by any rational measure. But I could no longer take pride in them. Pride had been the engine of my identity, and the engine had been dismantled and replaced with a perpetual hum of existential horror.\n\nThe worst part was that Godric remained the same uncle I had always loved. He asked about my studies, ruffled my hair, told me I was working too hard. And every kind word from his lips now felt like a velvet-wrapped dagger. Because I knew. I knew that if he wished, he could unmake me without even forming a deliberate thought. I knew that all my lineage\u2019s magical prowess was a gift\u2014the Awakening that multiplied our power daily\u2014and that this gift came from him, though he never said so. I knew that my father\u2019s father\u2019s father, all the way back to Blake, had served not as a shield but as a companion, a pet, a friend, a child. And that truth, once seen, could not be unseen.\n\nI stopped sleeping well. I would lie awake, staring at the ceiling, and in the dark, I would replay the moment of Azarak-Vos\u2019s unraveling. Not because it was gory\u2014though it was\u2014but because of what it represented. The absolute inability to oppose. The fact that the very act of raising magical intent against the king had not just failed but had triggered a corrective response so disproportionate that it annihilated the very concept of magical capacity in an entire universe. And even that was a mercy, because Godric had chosen not to unmake the Zyraki themselves. He could have. With the same zero effort, he could have unmade them all, then unmade the memory of them, then unmade the possibility of them ever having existed. And it would have cost him less than a blink.\n\nOne evening, I found myself in the royal library, the same study where, as a boy, I had sat on Godric\u2019s knee while he read me tales of Olympus. The shelves of grimoires\u2014my ancestors\u2019 work\u2014felt like litanies of insignificance. I pulled down a tome that my great-grandfather had written on the theory of permanent warding, a text that had once filled me with reverence. Now the pages seemed to crinkle with dry irony. What did warding matter when the king could simply will the ward into irrelevance?\n\nGodric appeared in the doorway. He was holding a cup of tea, steam curling upward. \u201cYou\u2019ve been quiet lately, Gorm. More than usual. You\u2019re not still troubled by the Zyrak business, are you?\u201d\n\nI looked at him, this man who was my uncle in every way that mattered, and yet was also the most horrifying entity in the entirety of existence. \u201cYour Majesty,\u201d I said, my voice flat, \u201cI\u2019m trying to understand my place. If my magic means nothing to your safety, then what am I? A mascot?\u201d\n\nHe set the tea down and crossed the room. His hand found my shoulder again, the same grip that had stopped me from throwing my life away against Azarak-Vos. \u201cYou are my family. Your place is not defined by utility, Gorm. It\u2019s defined by love. I know that\u2019s not the answer your pride wants, but it\u2019s the truth.\u201d\n\nHe said it with such sincerity that I almost believed him. And that was the deepest horror of all: the love was real. He genuinely cared for me. He genuinely saw me as family. And still, I could not escape the knowledge that his love was the affection of a god for a mayfly, a warmth that coexisted with the absolute capacity to annihilate me in a way so thorough that not even the memory of my existence would persist.\n\nAfter he left, I stood alone in the library, surrounded by the accumulated arcane lore of eighty millennia. I extended my senses, trying to measure the divide between my magic and his. It was like trying to measure the distance between a single raindrop and all the oceans that ever existed. There were no numbers. There were no metaphors. There was only the cold, inescapable fact that I occupied a universe that existed entirely at his sufferance, and that his sufferance was as eternal and unchanging as his affection. The fact that I loved him back, that I would still lay down my life for him if it could somehow help\u2014that fact was the final, hopeless irony. Because my sacrifice would be as pointless as everything else.\n\nOpposing Godric was not an act of defiance; it was a form of worship that fed him. Any soul foolish enough to raise a hand against the king would discover, as Azarak-Vos had discovered, that their rebellion was predestined to fail, that the very thought of opposition triggered a cascade that made Godric even more invincible than before. And after the failure, if the king was merciful, he might grant them a quick annihilation. If he was not, they would become a soul-stone, a pocket of eternal torment, a monument to the futility of resistance.\n\nI placed the tome back on the shelf. My hand trembled\u2014not from fear of the king\u2019s retribution, because I was loyal and always would be, but from the sheer, vertiginous insignificance of my entire existence. I was a court wizard, the pinnacle of mortal magic, and my magic was a mote of dust in a hurricane that had no end. I would serve for the rest of my life, and every day, the king would greet me with warmth, and ask after my family, and I would smile and answer him, and the entire time, the space between us would be the space between a neutrino and the star that birthed it.\n\nOutside the window, the capital of Thronegate glittered under the light of a million stars. Somewhere in the palace, Godric was probably reading a report or chatting with a servant. He was, beyond all argument, the best king the omniverse had ever known. He was kind, just, fatherly. And he was the abyss. The two truths were not contradictory; they were a single, seamless whole. And I would have to live the rest of my days carrying the weight of that comprehension.\n\nThe night wind carried the distant, faint chime of a bell. Somewhere, a child laughed. Somewhere, a newly-subjugated universe signed its treaty of surrender. And in the library, the court wizard stood motionless, buried alive in a knowledge that had no antidote, knowing that the only thing worse than opposing Godric was being loved by him."
